The bomber has been arrested and is being interrogated by the police. The Catholic Sports Club in Salzburg and a building in the same city were also bombed and damaged. At the same time, there were two incidents on the border, both occurring in Vorarlberg, the westernmost region of Austria. The first incident injured an Austrian patrol officer. The second incident involved two Austrian soldiers from Bavaria who specialized in delivering letters between Munich and Vienna and were arrested by Czech gendarmes, who said that the two were carrying supplies for

Austrian Nazi propaganda and money. The intended recipient of the money has been detained in Vienna. (Reuters, 7th)

Britain Restricts Japanese Silk: Will Adopt Quantity Restriction Method: British Territories Act in Concert with Mother Country 54

(London) According to the "Financial News," the British government will adopt a quantity restriction method for silk imports in the short term. This matter has been decided, but special consideration will be given to French silk to avoid damage. The newspaper briefly stated, "The British government has decided to adopt this method. This is the first time that Britain has restricted the quantity of industrial goods imports. It will be implemented through special laws. However, it is not yet possible to determine whether the quantity restriction method will apply equally to silk products from all countries or will be limited to Japanese products. According to the government's intention, it is extremely desirable to prevent Japanese silk industry competition, but under certain conditions, there are difficulties in not hindering the import of French silk. According to the Anglo-Japanese Commercial Treaty, Britain cannot take discriminatory measures against Japanese goods in terms of tariffs, and if it wants to prevent Japanese competition through tariffs, it will not be effective unless the tax rate is raised to more than 250%. Therefore, it is better to adopt a quantity restriction method. The government has sought expert opinions on whether the quantity restriction method, if applied only to Japan, would constitute discriminatory treatment, and the experts' opinions vary. It is estimated that the government will apply it equally to all countries, but in order to take care of France, it will take the year most favorable to France and most unfavorable to Japan as the standard for determining the import quantity. The year that meets these conditions is 1930." (Havas, 8th) (Tokyo) According to Toho News, the government of Jamaica in the British West Indies has passed a bill in the second reading of its parliament to implement a quota system for imported silk and rayon fabrics, with the aim of restricting imports of Japanese goods. (United Press, 8th)

(Osaka) According to a telegram from Singapore received by the Osaka Chamber of Commerce, the Straits Settlements government has decided to submit this bill to the Legislative Council on the 11th of this month to resist Japanese cotton cloth and rayon fabrics, and it is expected to pass. The impact on Japanese cloth is very great. (United Press, 8th)

Dutch-Japanese Conference Opens: Representatives of Both Sides Deliver Speeches Encouraging Mutual Efforts to Enhance Trade Relations 55

(Batavia) The first formal Dutch-Japanese conference opened at the Art Association at 11:00 this morning. The Japanese side was represented by Representative Nagaoka, Consul General Koshida, and various advisors and staff members. The Dutch East Indies side was represented by Representatives Lanaufte and Von Linston, as well as various committee members. First, Mr. Lan gave an opening speech, the main points of which are as follows:

"Before the start of the conference, the turbulent atmosphere between the two countries has now calmed down. It is an excellent opportunity to proceed with the conference in a calm atmosphere. As for the matters that should be decided at this conference, it is not possible to say now. However, the actions of the Dutch East Indies must adapt to changes in the world situation, and there will be no offensive motivation. It is only necessary to respond to necessities and seek to protect itself. Future international trade must adapt to newly emerging events. Therefore, the Dutch East Indies will begin to conclude new agreements with various countries based on this policy. It has had trade relations with Japan for centuries, and it is a great honor to discuss this issue with Japan for the first time."

Next, Japanese Representative Nagaoka gave a reply, saying:

"At the luncheon, the Governor stated his views on Dutch-Japanese trade, saying that the Dutch-Japanese relationship has not changed to this day, and it will inevitably be pure in the future. I express my sympathy. The relationship between the two countries is permanent. As for economic life, it must be changed according to the situation, so it should not be confined to temporary phenomena, and exaggerate the value of it. Although it is appropriate to seek appropriate measures for temporary misfortunes, one must not forget the optimism of the future. If one discusses minor disadvantages and wastes time, it will shake the international order. Therefore, we must uphold the principle of coexistence and co-prosperity, the spirit of cooperation and compromise, and maintain a special friendly relationship in order to enhance the friendship between the two countries. We intend to approach it with the best of efforts."

After the speeches, the Dutch side proposed that the agenda of future meetings should be decided after further consultation. The meeting ended here, but the representatives of the two countries continued to hold informal consultations to discuss the agenda and procedures. The Japanese side hopes that before discussing specific issues,

the Dutch East Indies will abolish the import restriction order. Therefore, depending on the Dutch side's approach, waves may occur at the beginning of the meeting. The date of the second meeting has not yet been decided. (Denstu, 8th)

Japanese Goods Penetrate Everywhere: Develop Towards Central and South America: Cotton Textiles Occupy an Important Position 56

(Washington) Japanese goods exported to South America in 1933 increased threefold compared to 1931. Japan's commercial progress in Argentina, Peru, Brazil, Chile, Uruguay, and other countries is very rapid. Japan's woolen textile industry in 1933

purchased a large amount of wool from Argentina and Chile, thus forming a balance of reciprocal commodities. However, this balance ultimately benefits Japan. Among the goods exported from Japan to South America in 1933, cotton textiles occupied the most important position, especially cotton textiles exported to Argentina. Cotton textiles exported to Argentina in 1933 amounted to approximately 6,616,000 Japanese yen, while in 1931 they were 1,408,000 Japanese yen. Japan's trade in Central America is developing even faster than in South America. It also profits greatly in Cuba, Mexico, and the Panama Canal Zone. Japan has a large trade surplus in the Central American region. In 1933, Japanese goods exported to Central America totaled 16,175,000 Japanese yen. In the same year, Japanese goods imported from Central America were worth 438,000 yen. Although Cuba and Mexico purchased large quantities of Japanese goods,

the two countries' goods failed to be imported into Japan in large quantities. (National, 7th)

(Moscow) The Soviet government is now banning trivial official documents. From now on, officials who are good at writing will either be imprisoned or sent to Siberia. The most difficult thing for government agencies is the endless number of reports and statistics, many of which have never been reviewed despite being thick. The paper and time spent each month are enormous. The People's Committee has paid attention to the current situation. The People's Committee criticized trivial reports as a strange phenomenon of bureaucratic politics, and instructed all departments not to report casually unless absolutely necessary. The Soviet Supervisory Committee has been ordered to severely punish officials who sabotage the above instructions. (National, 8th)

Roosevelt's Silver Bill: Fierce Debate in the Senate: Said to Hinder Economic Recovery: Rogers to Investigate Bank of Japan, Will Come to Shanghai Again 61

(New York) President Roosevelt's silver bill is now being debated in the Senate. Most people are now fiercely protesting against this bill, even saying that it is enough to delay the realization of the American economic recovery. The Finance Committee of the New York Chamber of Commerce submitted a report stating that the proposal to raise the price of silver cannot be realized without cooperation with other countries, and that the New York Chamber of Commerce should oppose this proposal. The report particularly criticized the provision in the silver bill that levies a 50% tax on silver trading profits, saying that its result is enough to hinder the New York market and allow the London and Shanghai markets to profit. (Havas, 7th)

(Nanjing) In order to support President Roosevelt's silver policy countermeasures, Professor Rogers, who was sent to China to investigate currency policy and economic conditions, will meet with Tsushima Shuichi, Director of the Finance Bureau of the Ministry of Finance, on the 9th, and then go to Shanghai again. At the end of the month, he will come to Japan again to meet with Minister of Finance Takahashi and Governor of the Bank of Japan, Hijikata, to inquire about Japan's policy on currency issues. (Dentsu, 8th)

President Lincoln Ship: Escapes Danger, Arrives in Honolulu: Carelessness in Cargo Hold Suspected Arson: Passengers Calm and Safe 62

(Honolulu) The President Lincoln, a ship of the Dollar Steamship Company, caught fire in its No. 7 cargo hold yesterday, and a radio warning was issued. This morning, the ship arrived here under its own power, escorted by a Coast Guard cutter and a Navy fireboat. Although the President Lincoln showed no signs of fire, lifeboats had been lowered, and some passengers were still wearing life jackets. The fire in the burning cargo hold had not been completely extinguished, and the fireboat was still pouring water on it. The public

believes that the cargo was heated and caught fire on its own, but the captain suspects that someone set the fire in hopes of destroying the ship. According to passengers, after receiving the fire alarm signal after dinner, they entered the lifeboats together, not panicking at all, and sat quietly in the boats to wait. It was not until midnight that they learned that the danger had disappeared. An Englishman, Brown, was one of the passengers. He told a Reuters reporter about the fire, saying that thick smoke spewed out from the cargo hold, blinding people. The lifeboats were lowered one after another, ready for passengers to board in case of emergency. The passengers all put on life jackets, and everything was very orderly, with no panic. A British woman, Mrs. Hansford, said that the ship's band was still playing music when the fire broke out, and some passengers were even dancing, while the crew tried their best to comfort the passengers, saying that there was no reason to panic. The President Lincoln departed from New York on May 10 for the Far East, carrying 60 passengers and a crew of 200. After discovering the fire in the cargo hold, it immediately sent out a distress radio. Before long, several merchant ships and warships rushed to help, but upon arrival, they learned that the fire had subsided and was not worth worrying about. (Reuters, 8th)

(Honolulu) The Dollar Steamship Company's President Lincoln was careless yesterday. Because the ship was carrying two aircraft purchased by the Chinese government from the United States, they were unloaded and inspected after arriving in Honolulu. The English newspapers here reported that the cause of the fire was related to the aircraft. (Japan United Press, 8th)

Japan Seeks to Negotiate the Arrangement of Old Debts with Our Country; The Principal and Interest Amount to 700 Million Yen; Sakanishi Takes on the Mission of Negotiating the Nishihara Loans 97

A report from Beijing: In order to arrange the Nishihara Loans, the Japanese side has recently been actively using Wang Yitang to restore the China and Foreign Trust Bank and sending Uchida to China to negotiate with our country. Uchida has now returned to Japan to participate in the Nishihara Loans arrangement meeting jointly organized by the East Asia Industrial Development Bank, the Korea Bank, and the Taiwan Bank. It is reported that he will come to China again immediately after the meeting. As for Sakanishi, an important figure in the Japanese military who has been active in the Pingjin area, he has gone south from Pingjin a few days ago and also has the mission of negotiating the Nishihara Loans with our country. Sakanishi is currently in Shanghai and is reportedly actively working and will visit Duan Qirui, Huang Fu, and others to discuss this matter. It has recently been learned that Sakanishi visited important figures in our country a few days ago and discussed the Nishihara Loans and the restoration of the China and Foreign Trust Bank. The current National Government Executive Yuan authorities are working with relevant agencies to review the principles of arranging foreign debts. The Foreign Debt Arrangement Committee will also be restored soon. Therefore, the Japanese side has decided to make every effort to negotiate the arrangement of old debts. Ambassador Arichi, who is returning to China from Japan, has also been instructed to focus on arranging old debts in his negotiations with our country. This policy of the Japanese side is worthy of attention. It is also learned that the Japanese side claims that the total amount of old debts, including principal and interest, is 734,770,000 Japanese yen. According to its content, the Ministry of Finance owes 142,354,000 Japanese yen, the Railway owes 164,209,000 Japanese yen, the Ministry of Communications owes 75,600,000 Japanese yen, military loans amount to 102,559,000 Japanese yen, and the industrial sector owes 245,090,000 Japanese yen. Among these old debts, the Nishihara Loans are the largest and the most difficult to arrange. The Japanese side has decided to first raise the issue of the Nishihara Loans and negotiate with our country in the hope of obtaining a definitive guarantee. According to the Japanese announcement, the so-called Nishihara Loans include a 20 million yen loan from the Bank of Communications, a 20 million yen loan for wired telecommunications, a 10 million yen loan for the Jihui Railway, a 20 million yen loan for participation in the war, a 20 million yen loan for the Shandong Railway, a 20 million yen loan for the four Manchurian-Mongolian Railways, and a 10 million yen loan for the Jilin-Heilongjiang Forestry and Mining Railway, totaling 140 million Japanese yen. Counting the interest over the past 17 years (the year the loan was established was 1918), it amounts to about 300 million Japanese yen. (Huate News Agency)

Poisonous Atmosphere Permeates Luan East: Japanese and Korean Rogues Set Up Drug Institutions Everywhere; Daily Sales of Drugs Valued at 300,000 Yuan 98

A Tianjin correspondent reports that in recent months, the Japanese have been making every effort to sabotage various facilities in the counties of Luan East, so that the area falls into a state of permanent unrest, the people cannot catch their breath, and the source of chaos will naturally grow, from which Japan can profit. The most vicious of these plans is that within the 23 counties in the war zone, a poisonous atmosphere has spread everywhere. Institutions for selling morphine, heroin, opium, and gambling, even in the smallest villages and towns, have two or three establishments. The operators are all Japanese and Korean rogues who rely on extraterritoriality and the current special power of the Japanese to run rampant in cities and counties without any scruples. Although the Japanese side has repeatedly received our protests, they superficially promised to restrain them, but secretly helped the rogues expand. Even the transportation of drugs is often escorted by the official Japanese army, openly transporting them in military vehicles to supply various places. Local authorities have no recourse because the Japanese are unreasonable. According to a survey by the Provincial Government, the most severely affected counties include Fengrun, Changli, Luan County, Laoting, Linyu, Tang County, Zunhua, Qian'an, Lulong, and Funing, with an average of no less than 300 drug institutions in each county, for a total of more than 3,000 in the ten counties. Each drug institution sells an average of about 80 yuan of drugs per day, for a total of about 300,000 yuan per day. This is all cash flowing out, absorbed by the Japanese side to go away, so the people of each county are poor and the economy is exhausted to the extreme. Although the two wheat crops have been sown so far, farmers are addicted to smoking and gambling, resulting in the loss of cultivation. The amount of abandoned farmland is innumerable. The wealth in deserted villages has been exhausted, and even those who offer high-interest loans have nowhere to borrow money. The Provincial Government is quite concerned about the desolate conditions of each county and has instructed local magistrates to negotiate, but the Japanese side does not take it seriously. When the Provincial Government negotiates directly, the Japanese side equivocates, so there is no solution. In addition, the Japanese have recently ordered the puppet Ministry of Finance Salt Affairs Department to dump Yingkou salt in the war zone and eastern Chahar, greatly reducing prices. Salt is the basis of the people's food and a major source of revenue for our Lux salt tax. Since the dumping of puppet salt, the position of Lux salt has deteriorated. The revenue from Lux salt donations in May was only over 900,000, more than 700,000 less than in the same month last year and more than 300,000 less than last month. It can be seen that the invasion of puppet salt cannot be ignored. (6th)

Changsha City Chamber of Commerce: Opposing Additional Militia Levies; Additional Levies Violate Established Practice, Merchants Find Burden Unbearable 100

Changsha Correspondence: Since Hunan Province successively established the Hunan Provincial Pacification Headquarters and the Security Command Headquarters and other agencies to be responsible for consolidating the militia defense of various counties, five or six years have passed. The entire province has been divided into six security districts, each governing several counties or as many as one or twenty counties. The militia defense within each district has been uniformly reorganized according to the national military system, with regiments as units, abolishing the original county boundaries, using numbers as serial numbers, and unifying the organization. In total, the militia teams of 75 counties in the province have been reorganized into 24 security regiments, one independent battalion, and one special service battalion. Previously, militia levies were managed independently by each county, but now they are uniformly collected by the government, specifically by adding five yuan to each tael of regular land tax, which can collect more than four million yuan annually. Additionally, a militia levy of two jiao is added to each mu of lake land, which can collect more than 800,000 yuan annually. The total of both items can collect five million yuan annually for application. Recently, the entire Fourth Route Army entered Jiangxi to suppress bandits, and the security of the Hunan border relies on the maintenance of these security regiments. A Militia Levy Supervision Committee was separately established within the Security Command Headquarters, with the government hiring one impartial gentry member from each of the six security districts to form the committee, supervising the revenue and expenditure of militia levies to demonstrate transparency. Currently, the committee anticipates that the revenue and expenditure of militia levies will be short by several hundred thousand yuan, so it has submitted a request to the government to increase three additional levies to supplement the funds: (1) add 10% to the production and sales tax, (2) add 30% to the business tax, and (3) add 30% to the brokerage tax. The Changsha City Chamber of Commerce, upon hearing the news, believes that the increase in militia levies would be difficult for merchants and residents to bear, and has risen up in opposition, telegraphing chambers of commerce in various counties and cities to jointly strive for a denial from the provincial government. The original petition states: "We learned from a report in this city's newspaper on the 24th of this month that the Hunan Militia Levy Supervision Committee proposed to add a militia levy of 10% to the production and sales tax in this province, and to add a militia levy of 30% to both the business tax and the brokerage tax. After reading this, we were extremely shocked. The militia levy has historically been added to the land tax of each county and has been in effect for many years. We have never heard of it being insufficient. Even if reorganization is carried out this time, it can only be to adjust the deficit and seek remedies under the land tax additions. It is absolutely impossible to violate established practice and increase the burden on merchants for no reason. Moreover, the production and sales tax is a disguised likin, and the tax rate is extremely high, which is not found in other provinces. Merchants endured temporary pain to alleviate the government's financial difficulties, which was a matter of expediency and originally unavoidable. However, since its implementation, merchants' capital has been increased accordingly, the people's purchasing power has weakened, and the commercial arena has declined day by day. Last year, another 20% was added. Merchants felt that the government did not care about the people's hardships and was taking an inch after gaining a foot, and their dissatisfaction had been simmering for a long time. They had hoped that the situation would become slightly more stable, the treasury would become slightly more abundant, and the government could fulfill its previous declarations and resolutely cancel the tax to show great faith. Unexpectedly, the Hunan Militia Levy Supervision Committee suddenly made this proposal. If it is implemented, it will not only put the commerce of this province in dire straits, but the regular tax will also be affected, resulting in a shortage of income. As for items such as brokerage tax, post fees, and public welfare donations, the burden is already considerable. At a time when the rural economy is bankrupt, various production and sales are sluggish, and brokerage firms are closing down, which is frequently heard. As for the business tax, the tax rate set in this province is also heavier than in other provinces, and Article 8 of the business tax law promulgated by the central government already stipulates that no additional taxes may be levied. We merchants are suffering from the layering of donations and taxes, and the pursuit of public bonds, and we are exhausted and unable to bear any more burdens. The gentlemen of the Militia Levy Supervision Committee are respected by the locality and must be aware of the suffering of merchants and residents. Why do they recklessly disregard this and adopt this measure of draining the pond to catch all the fish, which harms the people in the name of protecting them? After the association convened an executive and supervisory meeting for discussion, it was resolved to petition the provincial government to deny the additions and to send a letter to the Hunan Militia Levy Supervision Committee to voluntarily withdraw the record on file. In addition to separate letters, we hereby respectfully submit this petition for supervision and implementation in order to alleviate the difficulties of merchants and maintain the tax policy." (27th day)

Shandong Silkworm Cocoon Season Has Arrived; Sales Have No Way Out, the Scene Is Miserable 101

Jinan Correspondence: The silk industry in Shandong Province has been depressed for years, with accumulated unsold stock. Silk merchants are suffering greatly, and many have even gone bankrupt due to financial difficulties. Therefore, since last year, silk factories in Yidu, Linqu, Changshan, and other counties with the most abundant cocoon production have completely closed down. When cocoon farmers carry their loads by cart to the factories, they are all rejected. Only the Japanese Suzuki Silk Factory buys them, but the supply exceeds the demand, and the Japanese make things difficult in every way. The value has been reduced to the lowest possible level, and cocoon farmers all endure it with their heads bowed. Later, Suzuki also refused to buy, and on the day it stopped buying, cocoon farmers carrying loads in carts stretched for several miles, sleeping outdoors for several nights, begging the Japanese to buy, but ultimately to no avail. Cocoon farmers all left in tears. This year, the Department of Construction believes that the silk industry is still inactive, and the resumption of silk factories is uncertain. Silkworm farmers have no way to sell. In order to provide relief, it plans to use the government's power to encourage farmers to organize cooperatives to sell on their behalf, to bake cocoons on their behalf to prevent moths from emerging, and to introduce bank loans so that cocoon farmers can be relieved. The plan is very thorough. The department sent technician Chen Shican, who is currently traveling to Yidu, Linqu, Changshan, and other counties to actively carry out the plan. According to Chen's report to the Department of Construction, new cocoons have been seen in Changshan and Yidu, and in three days, it will be the peak season. Linqu is later, and in about a week, it will also be the peak season. Currently, the cocoon price is 2 jiao and 2 fen per jin for white cocoons in Yidu (each jin of cocoons purchased in various counties is 24 liang), and 1 jiao and 8 fen per jin for yellow cocoons. Linqu is roughly the same. Zhoucun, because there is a need for local silk reeling factories, is 2 jiao and 1 fen per jin. In Yidu and Linqu counties, no Chinese silk factories are buying. The only one offering to buy is the Japanese Suzuki. Judging from this year's situation, there are still many silkworm farmers, but the number of buyers is limited, and there is no way to sell. The situation is even more miserable than last year, and relief is urgently needed. Regarding the issue of bank loans, the Bank of China has sent a special commissioner for rural lending, Yan Kelie, from the head office, who is currently in Yidu to negotiate. The bank is semi-automatic in nature and plans to set up temporary warehouses, mortgage loans, and bake and store cocoons on behalf of cocoon farmers. Doing so may provide some relief. As for organizing cooperatives, technicians from various counties have come one after another to organize offices in various counties. Farmers are all delighted and enthusiastically organizing. The degree of need is similar to that of the Qidong Cotton Industry Cooperative. Currently, there are 4 societies and 14 offices registered in Changshan, 27 offices in Yidu, and more than 200 offices in Linqu. More than 1,000 registration forms for voluntary organization have been collected. However, because the matter is urgent, if all the organizational work is carried out according to the formal procedures, it may delay the cocoon season. Therefore, the situation will be considered and handled in order to be rapid.

The Eight Provinces' Security Conference Concludes; Attendees Visit Various Defense Works 102

Nanchang Correspondence: Chairman Chiang Kai-shek convened the security directors of Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, Jiangxi, and Hunan provinces, as well as the regional security commanders of each province, for instructions at the Nanchang headquarters. The meeting was held on the 1st. There were no proposals at the meeting, and it was entirely focused on reports. On the morning of the 2nd, the security directors of each province completed their reports to the general assembly in turn. Then, Chiang delivered instructions, roughly saying, "The people's militia and police force are the basic military force of the people, and they should be strictly reorganized and trained to strengthen self-defense. The training of the people's militia should not only be limited to shooting and combat, but also require the teams to understand the current position and environment of our country so that they can faithfully perform their duties. The people of our country have little knowledge and lack organization and training. The training of the people's militia and baojia should start from small things. If each county can train 400 people each year, it will also be quite considerable in a year," and so on. The instructions lasted for more than an hour, and the meeting closed around 12:00. In the afternoon, the headquarters held a public banquet for the attending members in the auditorium and showed movies for entertainment. The meeting adjourned at 10:00 in the evening. It is said that the headquarters received more than 70 reports and suggestions from the security departments and regional commanders of each province. Each province and region gave detailed reports on the situation of local red bandits, the progress of operations and suppression, the general situation of the people's militia and police force, and the implementation of the baojia and people's organization. They also made various suggestions on the aftermath of bandit suppression, the reorganization of teams, the training of baojia, and self-defense facilities, etc. These have been compiled into a book, and after adding general comments and instructions, they will be distributed to each province for reference, either to follow and imitate, or to make corrections. Currently, the participants are still visiting the city defense works and all construction projects in the province. They plan to visit the front lines and then return to their respective duties. Changshu: Inside Story of Cracking Down on a Large Opium Trafficking Organization 114

Qian Zhefu of Tianning Temple Lane in this county is a well-known opium trafficker in the county, but he is quite alert and has not been caught. His home has multiple mechanisms specifically for storing opium. The source of the opium is directly transported by steamboat from Shanghai, unloaded in the middle of the night, so few people know about it. On the 7th of this month, according to local reports, a patrol officer from the First Branch of the Public Security Station, acting on a tip, went to the Qian family and seized more than 40 packages of opium. The next day, the county government, acting on another tip, sent bailiff Lu Fusheng and others to the Qian family and cracked three mechanisms, seizing more than 800 packages of opium, and arrested his clerk, Shen Shulin, and Qian's wife, Gui, and brought them to the county. According to the confession, they do not traffic opium. Qian Zhefu works as a lawyer's assistant in Shanghai and does not often return home. The opium seized was inherited from his ancestors and stored here, etc. As a result, the two were detained. In addition, a fugitive, Qian Zhefu, was being arrested. However, the First Branch of the Public Security Station suddenly denied the opium seizure the day before and reported to the General Bureau for a review, saying that the report was inaccurate. However, Qian's neighbors in Tianning Temple Lane firmly stated that the opium was seized two days before and a large amount was taken away. According to a general rumor, on the afternoon of the 6th, the Qian's opium mechanism was cracked by the First Branch, which was indeed the case. However, afterwards, three tycoons came forward to intercede, asking for a fee of 5,000 yuan. As a result, 3,000 yuan was agreed upon. 1,600 yuan was paid in advance on the same day, and the remaining amount was promised to be paid on a later date. Unexpectedly, the tycoons embezzled 1,000 yuan and only distributed 600 yuan, resulting in unequal distribution, causing internal strife, and secretly reporting to the county government, resulting in the second major search.

Falsely Accused of Theft, Young Man Commits Suicide by Drowning 126

Zhang Baokang, a young owner of Juxing Tofu Shop at No. 256 West Avenue in this city, was 24 years old. He previously served as a squad leader in the 3rd District Security Corps of this city. He was imprisoned after being falsely accused of being an accomplice in a theft by the thief, Zhang Ashi. Later, after a second trial by the court, he was released on bail of 500 yuan. Because the court scheduled another summons for the 7th of this month, Baokang, overwhelmed with shame and indignation, took advantage of the Xinjiang Tianlun wheel departing from Ningbo the other day. A suicide note addressed to his father was left on the ship. Upon hearing the news, his family members wept bitterly.

Special Report: Impressions of Economic Survey in Guangxi Province (Continued) 127

We spent a total of fifteen days surveying in Guilin before departing for Pingle. Pingle is located at the confluence of the Gui River and the Le River. Goods coming from Wuzhou often arrive in Pingle first and then go to Guilin, so commerce is quite developed. Among the agricultural products here, hemp is particularly noteworthy. The simplest use of hemp is for twisting ropes and threads. A more advanced use is for weaving hemp cloth or making imitation wool. It is said that growing hemp requires little labor and fertilizer. After the hemp roots are planted, only some pig and cow manure is needed. There can be three or four harvests a year, and it does not require fertile land. The hemp harvest is usually around April or May (as the saying goes, "Good hemp doesn't last past April 8th"). This is precisely the time when farming families are between harvests, so it plays a significant role in regulating rural finance. One of the main reasons why usury is less prevalent in Pingle is hemp cultivation. Its benefits are so great that credit cooperatives cannot hope to match them.

Lipu, a neighboring county of Pingle, is known for its taro production. Lipu taro and Tiansha pomelo are both famous products of Guangxi Province. This kind of taro is as large as a round pillow, with each tuber weighing about five or six catties. Having grown accustomed to the small taros of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, we were amazed by these large taros. After staying in Pingle for three days, we set off for Babu. Babu is a town in He County, about thirty miles from the county seat, but the essence of He County's commerce is entirely concentrated in Babu. Even the Guangxi Bank Guilin Exchange Office has an office stationed there. We arrived during the Double Tenth Festival. It is said that the reasons for the decline of commerce in Babu are threefold: first, Cantonese salt cannot be sold to Hunan; second, unified donations are heavy and harsh; and third, the former County Magistrate Huang forcibly changed the market days to the Gregorian calendar. This reason is extremely ridiculous. Originally, the industries in Guangxi were still in the "market" system. They have a market every three days, which the Guangxi people call "xu". These market days are not uniform everywhere. Some are set on the 3rd, 6th, and 9th (held on the 3rd, 6th, and 9th days of the month), while others are set on the 2nd, 5th, and 8th. Often within a county, there are several major market towns, their distances being thirty or fifty miles, or sixty or seventy miles, and their dates being interconnected. On market days, all the farmers, peddlers, small industrialists, and small merchants...all gather together. Although it is not "exchanging what they have for what they need," it is truly "trading what they have for what is lacking and retiring after the transaction." On the day of the market, the entire village is often emptied. As for the traveling merchants, their lives are entirely based on going to the market. Today they go to this market, tomorrow they go to that market, and the day after tomorrow they go to another market. The "xu" is their only place to find customers, and folk customs are the center of their lives. He County is no exception, with several markets and market days, but since the former County Magistrate Huang took office, he issued a notice to change the market days to the Gregorian calendar. However, although the markets here used the Gregorian calendar, the markets in neighboring counties still used the lunar calendar. As a result, this market day conflicted with that market day. Farmers and peddlers could go to this market but not that market. Since the system of circulating markets was broken, farmers and merchants had no choice but to stop going to this Gregorian calendar market altogether. The commerce of Babu was also greatly affected by the change of market days. This passage proves that the promotion of new cultural systems, without overall planning and consideration, will inevitably repeat the mistakes of County Magistrate Huang.

The goods exported from Babu pass through the He River to Duch City. Duch City is a town in Guangdong, located downstream of Wuzhou and upstream of Sanshui. Goods produced in the He River often arrive in Duch City first and then are shipped upstream to Wuzhou or downstream to the provinces and Hong Kong. Economically, He County has an unusually close relationship with Guangdong, so the commercial and financial power of He County and Babu is entirely in the hands of Guangdong people. What is even more indicative is that the merchants and people here only use Dong Hao (minted in Guangdong) and Xi Hao (minted in Guangxi) are not welcome. Speaking of Guangxi's currency, this is also very interesting. Originally, both Guangdong and Guangxi used Hao Yang (small silver dollars) as the standard. Hao Yang is what we commonly see in the south with two horns, five of which are worth one silver dollar. The so-called "silver dollar" has become a virtual standard currency. Hao Yang has the status of legal tender in Guangdong and Guangxi. For example, if we want to borrow a thousand dollars from someone, if we want cash, they will give you five thousand double Hao. Otherwise, you can ask for exchange coupons issued by the provincial bank. If you must have Yuan Tou Yang or Sun Yang, you have to go to the market to buy them. The market price of Hao Yang compared to Da Yang is usually an extra thirty cents, or sometimes forty or fifty cents. There are two types of Hao circulating in Guangxi: one is Dong Hao, which is commonly used in Guangdong Province, used from 1912 to 1924; the other is Xi Hao, which is minted by Guangxi Province itself, also known as Jiahe Hao, only in 1926 and 1927. In addition, there is also a Zhongshan Yang, minted in 1929. However, it is extremely troublesome to use Hao in Guangxi. Merchants and people are too picky, and farmers often suffer losses. For example, Dong Hao is only commonly used from 1912 to 1920. They would rather carry hundreds or thousands of cumbersome copper coins than carry light and easy silver Hao or banknotes. Even the copper coins are made according to their own systems and are not unified. In some places, large copper coins (worth twenty) and small copper coins (worth ten) are used together and regarded as the same unit (one large copper coin equals one small copper coin), such as in Yongning. In other places, only large copper coins are used, and small copper coins are only used as a unit of calculation (one large copper coin is worth twenty copper coins). This is governed by Gresham's Law of "bad money driving out good money," and small copper coins have disappeared as a result, such as in Guilin. In other places, large copper coins are not used at all, such as in Wuzhou. However, there are even places where the price of small copper coins is higher than that of large copper coins, requiring three large copper coins to exchange for two small copper coins, such as in Beiliu. This is because large copper coins are not very common, so the price is lower. Copper coins are like this, not to mention Hao. What is commonly used in one place may not be used in another place. What is welcomed in one place may be rejected in another place. Generally speaking, the fineness of Xi Hao is better than that of Dong Hao. Because Xi Hao only existed in 1926 and 1927, there is very little private minting and counterfeiting, so it is especially welcomed by the people of Guangxi. But Babu is a special exception. Babu merchants are much more lenient in their pickiness about Hao than in other places in Guangxi. Almost any Hao (referring to Dong Hao) can be used, but they just don't want to use Xi Hao. It is said that this is caused by two conditions: first, the financial power of Babu is entirely controlled by Guangdong people; second, the power of Guangxi Bank has never reached this place before, and Xi Hao is issued by Guangxi Bank.

Guangxi's currency system is considered to be a relatively unified province. Exchange coupons issued by the Guangxi Provincial Bank can be used everywhere except in extremely remote villages. Although Hao and copper coins have their different usage habits in various places, there is no bad phenomenon of "each doing its own thing." There are only two situations that we consider to be the most worrying: The first is that farmers in the countryside of Guangxi still use copper coins as the standard. Because they have suffered two major lessons in the past (the Guangxi Bank banknotes were suspended once when Lu Rongting was in power in 1921, and again when Huang Shaoxiong was in power in 1929), they are wary of banknotes issued by the Guangxi Provincial Bank. Using Hao, and because merchants and shops are too picky, taking the opportunity to profit, so the result is that they would rather use cumbersome copper coins as the standard for all transactions, and the impact of the depreciation of copper coins has already caused them to suffer great losses invisibly. The second is that in Guangxi's neighboring counties bordering Annam, transactions are based on French Guang, and the national currency has regressed to a secondary currency status. French Guang is the currency commonly used in Annam. This kind of French Guang has great power in the border areas of Annam. Local residents have a twelve-point belief in French Guang, and Guangxi's currency must be discounted before it can be used. Although the Guangxi Provincial Government has repeatedly issued prohibitions, its latent power seems to be something that cannot be eradicated by a single order.

Guangdong Increases Agricultural Product Tax, Large Quantities of Grains Shipped to Guangdong, Three Cents Collected per Dan, Tax Collection Starts June 15th 134

Recently, the Guangdong authorities have increased the agricultural product tax, causing Cantonese merchants in Shanghai, Qingdao, and other ports to rush to load large quantities of grain to Guangdong. Within this week, 300,000 dan of various grains will be shipped. The details are as follows:

Collection of Agricultural Product Tax: To regulate the province's finances, the Guangdong authorities have decided to increase the tax on imported grains, called the Agricultural Product Tax. Calculated per dan, regardless of soybeans, rice, or wheat, all agricultural products must be taxed. It has been determined that the import tax will be three cents of silver per dan, starting on June 15th as the first day of collection. Each ton will be taxed approximately five yuan. The Guangdong authorities have announced this and notified all grain merchants.

Rushing to Transport Grains: The Guangdong grain merchants received a telegram from Guangdong stating that the tax is inevitable and will be collected soon. After this, the cost of grains arriving in Guangdong will increase significantly. They instructed various merchants in Shanghai to quickly transport agricultural products such as soybeans, peanuts, white rice, and wheat that have already been purchased to Guangdong before June 14th to avoid paying this new tax. The Shanghai Cantonese merchants estimated that at least 300,000 dan of grains from Shanghai, Qingdao, Hankou, and Haizhou can be rushed over. They have been in contact with various shipping companies to arrange for ships in advance to load the determined agricultural products and arrive in Guangdong one day before the new tax is implemented. Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, China Merchants, etc., have all agreed to dispatch ships to rush to load in Shanghai, Qingdao, and other ports.

Sanbei Adds New Regular Route: The Nanhua route of the Sanbei Company originally did not have regular commercial ships, only temporarily operating once or twice a year. This year, it plans to add a South China route, with the large ships Taishan and Longshan operating as regular ships, to the ports of Shantou, Guangdong, and other places, and set up wharf warehouses. Recently, due to the Guangdong's increased agricultural product tax, the grain merchants requested the dispatch of ships to transport goods. The Sanbei Company took the opportunity to advance the opening of the South China route. Yesterday, the Taishan ship was dispatched for the first time as a regular ship, carrying passengers and loading agricultural grains, about 16,000 to 17,000 dan to Guangdong.

Overview of Sino-Japanese Trade in April: Total Imports to China 11.55 Million Yuan, Total Exports 6.26 Million Yuan 135

According to a Central News Agency report, the International Trade Bureau released an overview of Sino-Japanese trade in April yesterday, which is recorded as follows: In April of this year, the total value of Japanese exports to China was 11,554,046 yuan, including 385,988 yuan from Taiwan, a decrease of 1,913,734 yuan compared to the same month last year, and an increase of 805,857 yuan compared to March of this year. In addition, the total of 35,000 thousand yuan in April is still far from the 114,106 thousand yuan of the total exports to China from the United States in four months. It is obvious that Sino-Japanese trade has not reached a good level.

Goods Imported to China: In April, cotton cloth was still the most imported commodity from Japan to China, valued at 782,820 gold units, equivalent to 1,546,852 national currency yuan. Among cotton cloths, undyed cotton cloth was the most abundant, reaching more than 372,000 yuan. Coarse cloth, fine cloth, and bamboo cloth were also considerable, totaling more than 339,000 yuan. Other dyed yarns and foreign yarns also reached more than 254,700 yuan. Items such as foreign standard cloth and fine twill cloth were also not small, each reaching tens of thousands of yuan. The number of fish and shellfish was also not small, with a total value of 429,015 yuan. Rubber products had 413,193 yuan. Other items such as rayon and cement each had hundreds of thousands of yuan. However, rice and flour increased very little, each around tens of thousands of yuan.

Export Goods: In April, food and flour were the largest exported commodities, valued at 663,455 yuan. Cotton was also considerable, valued at 637,771 yuan. The item of cotton yarn more than doubled compared to the previous month, reaching 448,349 yuan. Other items such as coal and ore each reached more than 300,000 yuan. Bones and meats were also more than 200,000 yuan. However, due to the robbery in the Northeast, the number of beans was still not worth mentioning, only more than 79,000 yuan. In addition, there were no major differences. The total export value in April was 6,165,610 yuan, an increase of 1,501,118 yuan compared to the previous month, which can be said to be a good situation. Total Trade Deficit: In trade with Japan this month, the total trade deficit was 5,388,436 yuan, a decrease of 700,000 yuan compared to the previous month, and it is still a major country with a trade deficit. As for gold and silver, there were absolutely no imports. Exports, including silver coins and raw silver, were only worth 100 yuan, an extremely small amount. As for merchant ships, 193 Japanese ships imported, totaling 358,68 tons. 188 ships exported, weighing 341,242 tons.

China's Egg Exports Decline Year After Year; Egg Merchants Request Negotiations with Various Countries to Increase Egg Taxes 136

According to a Central News Agency report, in addition to silk and tea, eggs are also among the top seven exports for China's foreign trade, but in recent years, they have been declining. The period from 1928 to 1930 was the golden age of egg exports, and egg merchants had considerable profits. Subsequently, it gradually declined and is even worse now. The reasons are: first, the egg production of various countries has increased, resulting in price dumping; second, countries that need eggs have increased tariffs and restricted the import of Chinese eggs. A comparison of egg exports since 1930 is as follows: The total export value in 1930 was 79,710,940 yuan; in 1931, it was 58,827,838 yuan; in 1932, it was 44,302,413 yuan; and in 1933, it was 36,489,477 yuan. This year is even worse than last year. The declining situation can be seen from the export comparison over the past four years. At present, egg merchants are appealing to the Ministry of Finance to exempt egg exports from export tax and are requesting the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate with countries that have increased egg tariffs to remedy the situation.

Three Major Principles of the Anti-Drug Association for Prohibition of Opium Presented to the Government Yesterday 138

The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association held a commemorative meeting on June 3rd for opium prohibition and requested the government to earnestly prohibit opium. After it was reported in various newspapers, it is learned that the association has telegraphed the government and proposed three major principles for opium prohibition. The original telegram is transcribed as follows: "To Chairman Lin of the Nanjing National Government, President Wang of the Executive Yuan, Chairman Chiang of Nanchang, and Deputy Commander Zhang of Wuchang, esteemed sirs, the harm of opium to the country has lasted for a century, causing internal and external troubles, leading to the shaking and decline of the national foundation and people's livelihood. The late Premier's instructions and the Kuomintang's program both advocated strict prohibition without a doubt. Judging from the current situation, the only way out for our country is to resist Japan to save the nation and to prohibit opium to survive. Opium prohibition is a prerequisite for resisting Japan. With the current slump in national morale and the decline of national strength, the whole country is in a state of darkness and unable to extricate itself. How can we talk about resisting Japan and seeking self-strengthening? Furthermore, opium is the vanguard of aggression and a tool for extermination. The Japanese warlords are intent on invading our country and first send vagrants to spread poison everywhere. After occupying the three northeastern provinces, they immediately rushed to implement the opium monopoly. Colonial governments in various parts of Southeast Asia also use opium to control overseas Chinese and hasten their demise. The sinister plan is obvious to everyone. The current situation in our mainland is probably even worse than in the Northeast and Southeast Asia. At the recent International Opium Conference, the American representative strongly condemned our country for producing opium everywhere, with a total amount exceeding seven times the world's total, which will inevitably poison the whole world. The words may be excessive, but it is undeniable that our country's opium poppy seedlings have not been cleared. Even if the central government is determined to prohibit opium, the various institutions established by warlords in the inland provinces mostly regard this as a source of profit. The opium power is developing rapidly. To talk about prohibition is almost empty talk. Therefore, the proposition of collecting tax on opium prohibition and the proposal of open sale are rampant. Some use scientific opium prohibition as a slogan, and some advocate turning private into public to move people. However, these methods have been implemented repeatedly. The result is limited income and endless outflow of currency. There is tax collection, but no prohibition. It only makes the opium disaster spread more and more, creating opportunities for unscrupulous people to make money, which does not contribute much to the national treasury. The impact is that the country's reputation is falling, and foreigners are constantly criticizing. Internally, scholars are becoming increasingly corrupt, and ordinary people are suffering from hunger. Public opinion is rising, and people's hearts are disturbed. Those who rely on this to open up financial resources will suffer more than they gain. I believe this has long been observed by your esteemed selves. Our association has been engaged in anti-drug activities for ten years, running and shouting without daring to slack off. Although the environment is bad, we still adhere to our consistent stance and continue to fight without daring to slacken. Recently, Chairman Chiang accepted the suggestions of the general secretary of our association and closed the opium dens in Wuhan. Then, he issued an order to strictly prohibit potent drugs. The news spread, and the masses were overjoyed. However, the accumulated poison in the country has penetrated deep into the people. It seems that a fundamental solution to the prohibition should be carefully planned, and a long-term detoxification campaign should be promoted. My colleagues are willing to contribute their years of research results and the knowledge gained from domestic and foreign investigations and studies. Here are the following suggestions for your selection: (1) The government should hire several Chinese and foreign experts to form an Opium Prohibition Design Committee and invite representatives from countries that have no special interests in opium to participate. These experts should be qualified with a thorough understanding of opium agriculture and economic issues. Start with investigation and research opium prohibition methods that meet the needs of the facts based on the investigation facts. The government should provide various conveniences and protections for the investigation and designate personnel to carry out the planned program. The total amount of opium tax collected by the central and local government troops should be calculated. The committee should study other sources to compensate. It is said that the new tariff sources should not affect the people's livelihood and disturb social stability. (2) In handling opium prohibition, no matter which method is adopted, the principle of pure prohibition should be adopted. The government should express its determination to carry it out strictly, starting with the military and political personnel to restore the public's faith. For opium prohibition administration, the government should select high-ranking and pure individuals who have the strength and determination to prohibit opium and are trusted by the people to take charge of the opium prohibition, and should give them practical guarantees and necessary privileges to make it easier to achieve results. Otherwise, the person in charge may use opium prohibition to make profits and promote their personal goals. The fines for opium prohibition and all opium revenue must be avoided for military and political expenses and should be allocated to handle smoking cessation and anti-drug education funds. As for the vast territory of the country, it is not easy to prohibit it in one day. It seems appropriate to designate several provinces to take the lead to set an example for other provinces and show the determination to implement it. (3) In handling opium prohibition, the government should cooperate with the people's anti-drug movement to promote the movement, such as surveying opium poppy fields, arresting smugglers, prohibiting private sales, and cracking down on smoking, to seek thoroughness and effectiveness. These responsibilities can be undertaken by the anti-drug organizations in each county and the local public organizations to select fair people to form an opium prohibition supervision committee. In order to promote opium prohibition, the government should convene a national opium prohibition conference on a regular basis to gather the opinions of officials and the people to promote cooperation between the two parties. Here are three outlines compiled based on the results of the Shanghai June 3rd Opium Prohibition Commemorative Meeting. I sincerely request that you implement them to save the crisis. Opium prohibition is fortunate, our country is fortunate. President of the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association, Wang Jingqi, General Secretary Huang Jiahui, and all committee members kowtow together."

Lin Kanghou Hopes Banks Will Circulate the Rural Economy. The Current Investment of Millions is Too Small. 141

A reporter from the Ta Kung Pao met with Lin Kanghou at the Bankers' Association yesterday to discuss the recent situation of banks in this city investing in rural areas. The details are recorded as follows:

Collapsed State of the Rural Economy 142

According to Lin, since the founding of the Republic of China, domestic natural disasters and man-made disasters have not stopped, resulting in the decline of rural areas and the decline of the economy. Ordinary wealthy households cannot withstand the harassment and have flocked to Shanghai to take refuge. As a result, the rural areas have become even more unbearable, and Shanghai has become increasingly prosperous. This kind of abnormal development is worrying about the future. Money is like blood. Shanghai is like the brain, and the inland is like the limbs. If the blood of the limbs all enters the brain, the limbs will become stiff. And in the brain, there will be cerebral hemorrhage due to too much blood. If the above situation is not remedied, the future of the country is in danger.

Recent Situation of Bank Investment in the Inland 143

At present, the banks in this city have become slightly aware of this, so some bank managers have turned their attention to investing in rural areas in an attempt to restore the rural economy. The recent investment situation includes the investment in Northwest construction. The Southwest is also sending people to negotiate, and it is expected to be agreed soon. The negotiations in Sichuan have been settled. Branches have now been established all over the inland of Jiangsu to facilitate farmers' loans. Jiangbei Xuzhou and other places have now been covered. In Jiangxi, there is the government-run Four Provinces Farmers Bank to regulate the finances of the four provinces. The Xinjiang and Tibet regions will be dealt with in the second term.

Lin's Opinion on Investment 144

Lin continued, "I very much agree with the bank's investment in the inland rural areas to restore the rural economy. The brain should also send blood to the limbs so that they can move. At the same time, we should know that the country is based on the people. If the people are poor and no measures are taken to remedy it, it is tantamount to the limbs dying while the brain lives alone. What is the value of living? Therefore, taking this opportunity to invest in the inland rural economy is the basis for a rich country and a strong people. However, the current investment of the banks in the inland is only several million yuan, which is too small. I hope that the banks will enthusiastically invest in the inland."

The Amount of Spring Cocoons from Zhejiang is Decreasing Year by Year. 146

This year's Zhejiang spring cocoons transported by the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway have been contracted by the Huitong Transportation Company. Transportation began on May 16, with successive reports of loading from various stations to Shanghai. The cocoons are unloaded at both the North and South roads. As of yesterday, the South Station had received more than 7,700 packages of spring cocoons, and the North Station had unloaded more than 3,000 packages, for a total of more than 10,000 packages. According to the contractor, the number of cocoons transported has been decreasing year by year. This year is the last for spring cocoons to be transported by rail. It is estimated that there will be more than 30,000 packages. In previous years, there were 150,000 to 160,000 packages at the end of the season. Since last year, it has decreased to 50,000 packages. This year, it has decreased to more than 30,000 packages. There are two main reasons for this: (1) due to market conditions, farmers have reduced raising silkworms; (2) railway freight rates are more expensive, so cocoon merchants have switched to water transportation.

However, since the first-class car only has 16 seats, only the leaders of various industries related to railway transportation have been invited to participate. The previous proposal to invite reporters from various newspapers to visit has been cancelled.

The Review Committee for Books and Magazines of the Central Propaganda Committee Has Officially Started Working. The Address is No. 7 Shanghai Villa, Huanlong Road. 150

According to the Central News Agency, the Central Propaganda Committee believes that among the books and magazines published by bookstores, many have pure ideas, but there are also some that contain other functions and are enough to lure young people and society. In the past, party and government organs had to give separate restrictions on such books and periodicals containing functions, but bookstores and writers inevitably suffered losses after publication. Now, in order to carefully restrict publications, a Book and Magazine Review Committee has been organized to review the original manuscripts of literary, artistic, and social science books and periodicals, so as to avoid losses to bookstores and writers after publication. The committee has now been prepared internally and has selected No. 7 Shanghai Villa, Huanlong Road, French Concession, as the address, and officially started working on the 6th of this month. It is reported that the committee has telegraphed the Central Propaganda Committee, informing the Book Industry Association of this city to inform all bookstores to send the original manuscripts of literary, artistic, and social science books and periodicals to the committee for review in accordance with the Book and Magazine Review Measures. The Book and Magazine Review Measures of the committee are recorded as follows: Article 1. These measures are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 5 of the Organizational Regulations of the Book and Magazine Review Committee of the Central Propaganda Committee. Article 2. All books and magazines published by bookstores, societies, or authors within the territory of the Republic of China shall, before printing, submit the original manuscript to the Book and Magazine Review Committee of the Central Propaganda Committee (hereinafter referred to as the committee) for review in accordance with these measures. The aforementioned review matters shall be conducted on a trial basis in Shanghai first in accordance with the resolution of the 115th Standing Committee Meeting of the Central Executive Committee. Article 3. When submitting the original manuscript of a book or magazine for review, the applicant shall provide the following items: A. Name of the book or periodical; B. Name and address of the applicant; C. Name and address of the editor; D. Length and number of words. Article 4. All books and magazines submitted for review shall be given convenient and swift review by the committee. Article 5. If the content of the original manuscript of a book or magazine submitted for review is deemed inappropriate, it may be returned to the original applicant with an order to delete and modify it in accordance with the review opinions. If the entire text violates the provisions of Article 3 of the Standards for Reviewing Propaganda, and violates the restrictions of Article 19 of Chapter 4 of the Publication Law, the committee may submit the original document to the Central Propaganda Committee for verification. Article 6. The committee shall issue a review certificate to the manuscript of a book or magazine that has been reviewed and approved by the committee. Article 7. When publishing the manuscript of a book or magazine that has obtained a review certificate, the review certificate number shall be printed on the cover page to identify it. Article 8. The committee shall list the books and magazines that have been reviewed and approved by the committee and submit them to the Central Propaganda Committee for forwarding to the Ministry of the Interior for record. Article 9. If there are any matters not covered in these measures, the committee may submit them to the Central Propaganda Committee for revision. Article 10. These measures shall be promulgated and implemented by the Central Propaganda Committee.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Re-Telegraphs the Ministry of Finance to Correct the Tianjin Fresh Fruit Tax and Implement the Resolutions of the Financial Conference. 151

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Finance again yesterday, saying: "To the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing, esteemed sirs, the case of the previous submission from the Chamber regarding the illegal collection of fresh fruit taxes in Tianjin City was approved by your ministry on the 7th of this month in Document No. 1623, which stated, 'Received the submission and informed the Qinghebei Provincial Government to investigate and handle the matter promptly.' This Chamber respectfully investigated that the layer of confiscated goods being auctioned is already beyond the point of no return. Those that have been confiscated but not auctioned have also had the fruit and goods industry in Shanghai recommend a representative to agree with the contractor on a temporary bookkeeping method of paying a deposit. These are not the main points of the case. What this Chamber previously submitted a request for was whether the tax should be levied on the goods according to the tax regulations, and whether the vendors should be regarded as brokers and forced to pay the brokerage tax. These are all legal issues, not factual issues. Your ministry is responsible for the national tax administration and should have the power to interpret and decide, without the need for local officials to repeatedly investigate. Whether the brokerage tax deposit can be returned has been stipulated to be decided by the interpretation of your ministry. This is the most important key to this case. It is also noted that the proposals for sorting out local finances submitted by your ministry at the National Financial Conference involve six items related to the brokerage tax: (1) Brokers are not allowed to set up checkpoints in trading markets or block roads to collect commissions. (2) Direct buying and selling of goods and passengers are not allowed to be forced to join the industry. (6) Disguised collection of goods donations is not allowed. The Tianjin fresh fruit brokerage tax is exactly this kind of malpractice. The previous submission from this Chamber has detailed it. We request that your ministry verify the previous submission and correct it in accordance with this decree. The dispute in this case can be resolved. Otherwise, if local officials entrust it to the municipal government, and the municipal government entrusts it to the finance bureau, and they repeatedly submit reports, they will inevitably protect their situation that has been established for more than ten years, or even use the fact that the confiscated goods have been returned as a pretext to avoid the serious and take the light. Businessmen are still in trouble, and there is no fundamental solution, and it does not help the matter. This Chamber is obligated to buy its stupidity again. We beg you to review and instruct us to comply. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce kowtows."

The Japanese-Qing Steamship Company is doing its best to operate the upstream and downstream lines of the Yangtze River. At its peak, a total of 21 ships were operating. Since the outbreak of the Northeast and Shanghai wars, it has been affected by boycotts, and almost all ships have stopped sailing. The Japanese design to restore it was ineffective. In order to maintain the route, they reluctantly operated the four ships Fengyang, Xiangyang, Nanyang, and Luoyang between Shanghai and Hankou. Now, because the heat of the boycott of Japanese goods in the provinces along the Yangtze River has gradually decreased, and the opportunity to dump goods has come again, the Xinyang Maru has been sent to resume sailing between Shanghai and Yichang, the Dangyang Maru has been sent to sail between Hankou and Yichang, and yesterday, the Yunyang Maru was sent to sail between Shanghai and Yichang. It will sail from Shanghai for the first time today, mainly carrying Japanese goods.

Ningbo Compatriots Organize a Literature Society to Edit a Summary of Siming Books. The Address is on the Third Floor of the Compatriot Association. 155

Zhang Shou-yong, the former Vice Minister of Finance and a native of Ningbo, is a lover of ancient books and has the reputation of being a "bookworm." His residence, Yueyuan, has a rich collection of books, especially focusing on local literature. He is diligent in collecting, without distinction between cold and summer. In recent years, he has edited the Siming Series, which has been printed in four collections of A, B, C, and D. In addition, he learned that the predecessors in various counties of Ningbo, from the Han to the Qing dynasties, have been authors. The Siku Quanshu recorded in the former Qing Dynasty only recorded more than 200 species, and those that were not recorded were more than double that. He planned to compile a list of books owned by each collector, examine their versions, discuss their origins, and compile a summary of Siming books in the style of the Siku Quanshu Summary. He has joined forces with more than a dozen like-minded people, including Ye Zhuotang, Fang Shiru, Zhou Zhenqin, and Wang Boyuan, to jointly initiate and raise funds of several thousand yuan to use the original library room on the third floor of the Ningbo Compatriot Association as the address of the society. He has hired Xia Qiyu, a senior compatriot, as the editor-in-chief, and Zhang and Xin Jiangming will assist him at any time. It is reported that they officially started editing on the 1st of this month, with the goal of completing the book in three years. In the future, the younger generation of Siming will be able to learn from this book as if they were personally taught by their predecessors, benefiting the students to come. This is of great help to local literature, and this move by the people of Ningbo is enough to be a model for general teachers.

Gang Workers Gather to Cause Trouble in Longhua Town 163

The fuel used by the Shitai Silk Factory in Caohe Temple, west of Longhua Town, Shanghai, was contracted by the Shanghai Rongchang Coal Company to hire boats to transport it to the Jiangkou in front of the factory for unloading. The workers in charge of transportation were all managed by Hu Yuede, a Siyang native, who was assigned by the contractor Tang Renzhi. Recently, due to disagreements, the work was taken over by Lu Youren, a Taizhou native, who was assigned by You Renzhi. As a result, Hu and Lu harbored personal grudges and competed during work. At about 11:00 AM yesterday, several more coal boats arrived. Lu Youren feared that Hu would come to compete, so he reported to the local branch station and the Caojing District Security Corps, and each sent police officers to the scene to suppress them. At that time, Hu Yuede's side already had more than 20 workers, each holding a pole to compete for transportation. The Security Corps took Zhang Defa, Chen Rushan, and Li Shanzhang, the three ringleaders, back to the team and confiscated an ax. While they were being interrogated, Hu Yuede gathered more than 60 hooligans and surrounded and attacked Shen Miaochun, the platoon leader of the Security Corps who was suppressing them in front of the Baotai Silk Factory, and the team members Hu Youcai and Wu Fusheng, with a fierce momentum. Platoon Leader Shen had no choice but to draw his pistol and fire several shots into the air, while leading the team members to escape the siege. However, the workers followed and chased them to the front of the team headquarters. With an order, they rushed in and released Zhang Defa and the other three. The order was chaotic at that time. Wu Rugui, the captain of the team, ordered the team members to retreat temporarily in order to avoid misunderstandings. He reported to Liu Songjian, a patrol officer at the town's branch station, and Tang Chunrong, a police chief, who led the police to the scene to disperse them and take Hu Yuede and Song Dongnan, the two ringleaders, to the station.

Wu Zhengding, the director of the station, briefly questioned them. According to Hu Yuede's confession, he was 51 years old, from Siyang, and lived in the Beipiao Company. The work was contracted by the people to Tang Renzhi, and the pole strength was 80 cents per ton, but Tang only paid me 40 cents. So, since May 1st, I have agreed with Mao Chunpu, the manager of Rongchang Coal Company, to pay 50 cents per ton. However, Tang Renzhi now entrusted Lu Youren to transport the poles and did not allow me to work, instigated the Security Corps to open fire, causing the workers Song Dongnan and Qi Desheng to panic and escape, lost their footing and fell into the water. Now Song has been rescued, but Qi is still missing. He must have drowned. According to the worker Song Dongnan's confession, he was 28 years old, from Siyang, and his confession was roughly the same as Hu's. Director Wu believed that the workers gathered to cause trouble and dared to trap the Security Corps team headquarters. However, Qi Desheng had drowned. It should be investigated and verified before proceeding. Therefore, he prepared a document and sent it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Fire in Gaochangmiao Road Yesterday Morning: Fire Spreads to Neighbors, Arsonist Arrested 164

Yang Chenglin, a resident of Nanhui, Pudong, is over sixty years old. He runs a straw shop at No. 53 Gaochangmiao Road, Nanshi. The business is doing well, and he can maintain his livelihood. When the nearby police officer saw it, he immediately notified the fire brigades of various districts and quickly dispatched fire trucks to rush to the scene. Then, Su Xin, a patrol officer at the Gaochangmiao Branch of the Second District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, led the police to the scene to maintain order and investigate the cause of the fire. The arsonist Yang Chenglin was taken to the Hu District for interrogation.

Ding Cui, a young woman from Anhui, was married to Ding Xiangsheng, a fellow villager, by a matchmaker named Feng on the 17th day of the first month of the 13th year of the Republic of China.
